<review>Quirky cafe that is part of a small regional chain with about 5 locations that has been around for more than 15 years now. There is a large indoor dining area, as well as a patio with heaters and a fire pit for when it gets cold. This particular location is an odd mixture of quirky cafe and upscale to match the community around it. This covers both the decor and the food. I had a zucchini and goat cheese pizza that was cooked in a wood fire pizza oven and it was quite good. The rest of my family enjoyed salads and sandwiches that were appreciated and also included some unique flair. Prices are on the higher end of moderate, but the quality of the food was good. Lots of good info on their website to help you make your decision.< /review><pics>None</pics>< Rate>

<user>102798794754057024413<//user><Name>Adam J M Richards<//Name><Time>1375594466648</Time><Rate>5</Rate>< Text>
The food is superficially simple, but it's all organic and tastes good. The decor is interestingly French country with a live tree inside the restaurant itself. It's highly kid friendly, and they'll swap the fries for a number of healthy alternatives - just ask.  They have difficulty keeping stocks of cider, for some random reason.

It can be busy, but the wait is seldom longer than 15 minutes I find. Parking on days when there is a downtown event or the farmers market on Saturday lunchtime can be tricky.

The wait staff are usually very friendly and quick to correct an error. On a summer day or night the patio is nicely shaded and fire-pitted.

If you like ginger, the ginger cake with pumpkin ice-cream is to die for. A favorite go to is the thai chicken salad in any of its three sizes. The chicken noodle soup (ask for extra bread) is good, honest stuff (and I'm not usually a soup person).</Text>
